[2025-12-22T14:59:31Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Just want you to first read the incident if you don’t know of it already, it’s a beautiful anecdote. ↵ Q. X was the daughter of Y, who is the subject of this interesting anecdote. X used to write poetry, and it was these poetic exchanges that led to her brief affair with another poet Z (not important for the context of the question, don’t need a guess). This angered Y, who put her through a challenge. “Come up with a couplet that talks about mixing of black and white (black being a representation of Z, white of X) within 24 hours” or Y would kill Z. ↵ X kept trying the whole day to come up with something, but couldn’t. Towards the end of the day, she started considering killing herself to escape the agony of watching Z die, this prompted her servant/_kanees_ to start crying inconsolably. As she started crying, a teardrop fell on a paper with some writing on it, mixing the teardrop with ink, prompting X to write: ↵ Ba ashk-e bar safḥa-yi nama, ↵ Siyah dar safed yaki shud ↵ Meaning - from a teardrop I write this story, of how it mixed with ink and became one. ↵ Y couldn’t challenge this couplet, and in anger, imprisoned X instead of killing Z. ↵ Id X, Y.

[2025-12-23T15:33:22Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: Abul Hasan Qutb Shah was the eighth and last Sultan of Golconda. He spent his formative years as a disciple of renowned Sufi saint Shah Raziuddin Hussaini Qattal, commonly known as Shah Raju. Abul Hasan married one of the daughters of Abdullah Qutb Shah, the seventh Sultan, and became Sultan after his death. Shah Raju gave Abul Hasan the nickname “X Shah” to mean “benevolent, pious king.” Aurangzeb was intent on ending the Golconda sultanate and he succeeded 14 years into Abul Hasan’s reign. Mughal propaganda then painted Abul Hasan as an incompetent, despotic, and tyrannical king. As a result of this propaganda, Abul Hasan’s nickname in Urdu and Hindi now means the opposite of its original meaning. Give X.
